of Trustees, it being hereby determined and declared that the establishment of
said department and the appointment of a Superintendent thereof is necessary
and expedient for the best interests of the Village. Said Superintendent shall
qualify for office in the same manner as any elective official of the Village
and shall post such bond in such amount as may be determined by the President.
All necessary employees of said department shall likewise be appointed by the
President with the approval of the Village Board of Trustees. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-
8-2006)
7-2-2: RATES, CHARGES:
There shall be and there are hereby established rates and charges for the use
of and for the services supplied by the sewerage system of the Village as
follows:
   (A)   Sewer Charges (Per 1 Month Billing Cycle): As used herein, one unit of
use is one hundred (100) cubic feet (750 gallons) of water used. The unit
charge is based on domestic strength concentration of two hundred milligrams
per liter (200 mg/L) biochemical oxygen demand (BOD), two hundred fifty
milligrams per liter (250 mg/L) total suspended solids (TSS), twenty three
milligrams per liter (23 mg/L) ammonia (NH3-N), and four milligrams per liter
(4 mg/L) total phosphorous (TP).
      1.   Residential:
         (a)   Inside Village limits:
With metered water:
$15.00 minimum rate for up to 2 units used which shall be increased annually as
follows:
2020 $17.50
2021 20.00
2022 20.40
2023 20.80
2024 21.20
2025 21.60
2026 22.00
2027 22.40
2028 22.80
2029 23.30
2030 23.80
2031 24.30
2032 24.80
2033 25.30
 
$5.25 per unit (or part thereof) for all additional water used which shall be
increased annually as follows:
2020 $ 7.00
2021 9.00
2022 10.75
2023 12.50
2024 13.20
2025 13.90
2026 14.60
2027 15.40
2028 16.20
2029 17.10
2030 18.00
2031 18.90
2032 19.90
2033 20.90
 
Without metered water:
Flat charge of $54.00 per month for billing years 2019 through 2025 and $75.00
per month for billing years 2026 through 2033.
   (b) Outside Village limits:
With metered water:
Minimum rate for up to 2 units used shall be 150 percent of the metered water
rates inside of Village limits.
Rate per unit (or part thereof) for all additional water used shall be 150
percent of the metered water rates inside Village limits.
Without metered water:
Flat charge of $200.00 per month
      2.   Surcharge For Industrial And Other Nondomestic Strength Usage: All
rates for industrial and other nondomestic strength users will be established
by the Superintendent based on concentration and quantity of sewage. The bill
for flow will be the same as for domestic users. Nondomestic users with
wastewater discharged to the sewer system at concentrations greater than
domestic concentrations, as described above, in addition to charges for flow
will have additional surcharges based on strength (mass load). The user shall
be required to provide analysis and sampling as determined necessary by the
Superintendent in order to establish the concentration and amount of discharge
into the Village sewer system.
A surcharge for nondomestic strength discharge shall be charged on the
following basis:
 
BOD      $0.40 per pound
   TSS0.75 per pound
   NH30.80 per pound
   TP 7.50 per pound
 
      3.   Water Meters: Water usage shall be based upon meter readings
provided to the Village by the current water utility company. Users may receive
adjustments to their user charge bills for metered water not entering the
Village's sewer collection system by installing appropriate sewer or water
meters or negotiation with the Board of Trustees for a straight percentage
credit. Responsibility for initiating negotiations and studies for such a
credit rests entirely with the user.
      4.   Users Without Meters: All users not having a water meter or other
acceptable device for determining usage shall be subject to a fixed base user
charge in an amount determined by the Village. The Village shall consider
charges imposed on users having similar water use and wastewater
characteristics in determining said base user charge. The Village, at its
direction and discretion, may require a user receiving all or part of its water
from a private well or other source not metered by the current water utility
company or other public or private supplier of potable water to install at the
user's expense an appropriate metering device for the purpose of determining
usage.
   (B)   Multiple Occupancy: Provided further, in addition to the minimum and
flat charges stated above, an additional monthly charge of thirty dollars
($30.00) shall be made for each apartment, flat, place of business or family
unit exceeding one, in all buildings with only one meter, but containing two
(2) or more apartments, flats, places of business or family units, provided
that no additional charge shall be made for any vacant apartment, flat or place
of business which is vacant during an entire two (2) month period.
   (C)   Application For Service: No sewer connection shall be made to any
premises until an application therefor in writing has been made for that
purpose and filed with the Sewer Superintendent of the Village, stating the
purpose for which the services are to be used.
   (D)   Connection Fee: There is hereby established a sewer service connection
fee of one thousand five hundred dollars ($1,500.00) for residential users and
six hundred seven dollars ($607.00) per PE (population equivalent) for
commercial and industrial (nondomestic) users.
For a proposed connection that will generate one thousand five hundred (1,500)
gallons per day or more of wastewater, a connection permit from the Illinois
Environmental Protection Agency (IEPA) must be issued before the Village of St.
Joseph can issue a connection permit.
The fee for any connection that requires an IEPA connection permit shall be the
calculated population equivalence stated in the IEPA permit application times
the connection fee per PE.
For nonresidential buildings, the connection fee shall be the highest of the
calculated population equivalence for design average flow (based upon 100
gallons of sewage per day), five (5) day biochemical oxygen demand (based upon
0.17 pounds per day) or suspended solids (based upon 0.20 pounds per day),
times the connection fee per PE. The minimum connection fee for nonresidential
buildings shall be based upon 2.5 PE.
The sewer connection fee shall be due prior to connection, and in the case of
new building construction, the fee shall be due and payable at the time the
application for building permit is filed, and said sewer connection must be
completed within twelve (12) months of payment of the fee or any additional
time approved for applicable building permit.
   (E)   Payment: All charges must be paid on or before the date due, to the
Village Clerk at the St. Joseph Municipal Building.
   (F)   Review Of Rates: Rates shall be reviewed annually by the Board of
Trustees and as otherwise deemed appropriate to determine if the rates will
provide sufficient funds to pay future costs of operation, maintenance and
replacement, and to determine that the rates charged users are in proportion to
the costs of the services provided. If the funds are not sufficient or the rate
does not maintain proportionality as determined by the review, revised rates to
accomplish the same shall be adopted by the Board of Trustees by ordinance and
published and thereafter be in effect. User charge rates so enacted by the
Village by ordinance shall remain in effect until modified or rescinded by a
subsequent duly passed ordinance.
The users of wastewater treatment services may be notified periodically, in
conjunction with a regular bill, of the rate and that portion of the user
charges which are attributable to the wastewater treatment operation,
maintenance and replacement.
A Depreciation Fund shall be established and funds collected for replacement
shall be sufficient to replace sewerage system facilities and equipment
necessary to assure its continued efficient performance and to maintain the
capacity for which it was designed and constructed and unless otherwise
directed by the Board of Trustees, five percent (5%) of gross revenues shall go
into the Depreciation Fund. The Village shall maintain a depreciation
replacement schedule of all personal and real property, including residual
asset value, estimated remaining service life and the total annual replacement
costs. This schedule shall be evaluated as deemed appropriate. (Ord. 2019-1, 4-
9-2019)
7-2-3: LIABILITY FOR PAYMENT:
The owner of the premises and the occupant thereof and the user of sewerage
service, shall be jointly and severally liable to pay for the service on said
premises, and the service is furnished to the premises by the Village only upon
the condition that the owner of the premises, occupant and user of the service,
are jointly and severally liable therefor to the Village. Bills shall be
rendered to the user at the end of each two (2) month period and shall be
payable within thirty (30) days after the date of the original bill. For any
bills not paid by said due date, a penalty of ten percent (10%) of the amount
of the charges for current services shall be added and become due. (Ord. 2006-
9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-4: APPEALS:
The method for computation of rates and service charges established for user
charges in section
7-2-2 of this chapter shall be made available to a user or owner within ten
(10) days of receipt of a written request for such. Any error in the method
used or in the computations thereof shall be remedied by the Village Clerk
within ten (10) days after notification of a formal written appeal outlining
the discrepancies. In the event the Clerk and the user or owner cannot resolve
the disagreement, the Board of Trustees shall review said matter and render its
determination at the next available Board meeting. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-5: DELINQUENT PAYMENTS:
   (A)   Lien: In the event charges for sewerage service, including any penalty
then due, are not paid within thirty (30) days after the rendition of the bill
for such service, such charges and penalties shall be deemed and are hereby
declared to be delinquent, and thereafter such delinquencies shall become and
constitute a lien upon the real estate for which such services are supplied.
Statements rendered for such user charge shall be deemed notice to the owner of
the property served and shall state that charges not paid within said thirty
(30) days may result in a lien being filed on said real estate pursuant to 65
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-141-7. The claim for lien shall be made in the
form of a sworn statement setting out: 1) a description of the real estate,
sufficient for the identification thereof, upon or for which the sewerage
service was supplied, 2) the amount or amounts of money due for such sewerage
service, and 3) the date or dates when such amount or amounts became
delinquent. In all cases where the user charge has become delinquent and the
Village elects to file a notice of lien therefor in the Office of the Recorder
there shall be added in addition to the amount due the Village such charges and
expenses as are necessary and required to verify the legal description of the
parcel to which the lien is to attach, plus a sum determined by the Board of
Trustees as sufficient to cover the cost of preparation of such notices and
forms required. In each instance, the Clerk of the Village shall be authorized
and directed to include such additional costs in the amount claimed due the
Village in the notice of lien. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
   (B)   Enforcement: The Village shall be empowered to prosecute an action in
chancery to foreclose any lien filed pursuant to this chapter, or in the
alternative, resort to an appropriate action at law to collect unpaid user
charges, penalties charged under this chapter, interest thereon, as provided by
statute, and attorney fees incurred by the Village and court cost taxed by the
court, in each such action. The Village reserves the right to disconnect the
sanitary sewer serving the property for which the user charge bill has become
delinquent, or direct the water company to shut off the supply of water to said
premises, regardless of the action taken by the Village to collect said
delinquent bill, until the delinquent bill has been paid to the Village's
satisfaction. (Ord. 2011-11, 11-8-2011)
7-2-6: DISCONTINUE SEWER/WATER SERVICE:
   (A)   Disconnection: Anything in this chapter to the contrary
notwithstanding, the board of trustees shall have the right to revoke sanitary
sewer connection permits and/or direct the water company to shut off the supply
of water to designated premises in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter. Such disconnection and/or shutoff may be accomplished prior to or
subsequent to the filing of the lien set forth above. Said lien may be filed
before or after disconnection of sewer service, revocation of connection permit
or shutoff of water supply. The clerk may order sewer service to be
disconnected or water supply shut off to any user in accordance with the
following procedures:
      1.   Bills not paid within thirty (30) days of billing date shall result
in a late payment penalty in the amount of ten percent (10%) of the charges for
current services and a notice of delinquency will be sent by first class mail.
      2.   If not paid within thirty (30) days, then a second notice of
delinquency will be sent to the user and owner by first class mail and
certified mail advising of disconnection of sewer service and/or shutoff of
water supply unless past due amount and penalty is paid, or unless user or
owner requests a hearing within twenty (20) days of the date of second notice
of delinquency, or unless an extended payment agreement is entered into between
the village and the user or owner.
      3.   If past due amount plus penalty is not paid and no hearing is
requested within twenty (20) days of notice of violation, and no extended
payment agreement is agreed upon, then a notice of disconnection and/or water
supply shutoff may be sent, at any time thereafter, by first class mail to the
user and owner advising of the date after which disconnection and/or shutoff
will occur unless payment is received. Said notice shall also be hung on the
front door of the building located on said property.
      4.   In the event a hearing is requested, the user and owner shall be
notified of the hearing date by first class mail no less than ten (10) days
prior to the date of the hearing before the board of trustees.
      5.   At the hearing, the user and/or owner may present evidence disputing
the charges or the record of payments. The trustees shall make findings as to
the amount owed by the user and owner and shall set a date, no less than ten
(10) days after the hearing, by which said amount must be paid unless an
extended payment agreement is approved by the board of trustees.
      6.   If said amount is not paid by the required date, sewer service may
be disconnected or water shut off at any time thereafter without further
notice, or in the event an extended payment agreement was approved by the board
and payment is not received by the village in accordance with said agreement,
then a notice of sewer disconnection and/or water shutoff will be sent by first
class mail to the user and owner advising of the date after which disconnection
and/or shutoff will occur unless payment is received.
   (B)   Reconnection: All amounts charged under this chapter are due and shall
continue to be due hereunder, whether or not said sewer is disconnected and/or
water supply is shut off, and no sewer shall be reconnected or water supply
turned on until the village is paid in full all amounts due it including
charges owed by the village to the water company related to the water supply
shutoff, together with a one thousand five hundred dollar ($1,500.00) fee for
reconnecting the sewer (if the sewer was disconnected), and in addition, there
shall be paid to the village a deposit of fifty dollars ($50.00) for the first
sewer reconnection or turn on of water supply, and one hundred dollars
($100.00) for any subsequent reconnection or water supply turn on. (Ord. 2011-
11, 11-8-2011)
   (C)   Responsibility To Ascertain Charges: The nonreceipt by any parcel
owner of a bill or statement for user charges shall not be an excuse for
nonpayment or entitle the user to request an extension or deferment of the date
upon which payment is due or to avoid inclusion of penalties and interest. The
owner of the property against which a notice of lien has been recorded pursuant
to the terms of this chapter shall be deemed to have notice of the existence of
the charge and shall be responsible for ascertaining from the village all
amounts, if any, due as provided in this chapter and the payment thereof. (Ord.
2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-7: CLERK TO RENDER BILLS:
It is hereby made the duty of the village clerk to render bills for sewerage
service and all other charges in connection therewith, and to collect all
monies due thereon, and it is hereby made the duty of all officials of the
village to enforce payment of all unpaid bills and penalties in the manner,
form, time and procedure under the laws of the state of Illinois thereunto
enabling. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-8: FUNDS KEPT SEPARATE:
All revenues and monies derived from the operation of the sewerage system shall
be held by the village clerk separate and apart from the clerk's private funds
and separate and apart from all other funds of the village, and all of said
sums, without any deductions whatsoever, shall be delivered to the village
treasurer not more than ten (10) days after the receipt of the same, or at such
more frequent intervals as may from time to time be directed by the village
board of trustees. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-9: SEWERAGE FUND:
The village treasurer shall receive all such revenues from the sewerage system
and all other funds incident to the operation of the said system, as the same
may be delivered to the treasurer, and deposit the same in a proper fund(s) of
the village of St. Joseph. Revenues so deposited shall be disbursed as
appropriated by ordinance and approved by the board of trustees. (Ord. 2006-9,
8-8-2006)
7-2-10: RECORDS, ACCOUNTS:
The village treasurer shall establish a proper system of accounts and shall
keep proper books, records and accounts, in which complete and correct entries
shall be made of all transactions relative to the sewerage system, and at
regular annual intervals the village board of trustees shall cause to be made
an audit, by an independent auditing concern, of the books to show the receipts
and disbursements of the system. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-11: ACCESS TO RECORDS:
The IEPA or its authorized representative shall have access to any books,
documents, papers and records of the village which are applicable to the
village system of user charges for the purpose of making audit, examination,
excerpts and transcriptions thereof to ensure compliance with the terms of the
loan agreement and rules of any state loan. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-12: COPY FILED WITH COUNTY:
A copy of this chapter, properly certified by the village clerk, shall be filed
in the office of the recorder of Champaign County, Illinois, and shall be
deemed notice to all owners of real estate of their liability for sewerage
service supplied any owners, occupant or user of such services on their
properties. (Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-13: VALIDITY:
In the event any one or more of the provisions of this chapter, for any reason,
shall be held to be illegal or invalid, such illegality shall not render
illegal or invalid all other provisions of this chapter, and in every such
event this chapter shall be construed and enforced as if such illegal or
invalid provisions had not been contained herein. No portion or provision
hereof shall be taken to establish lesser or different requirements than those
imposed upon persons by the state and federal governments for purposes of
protecting and improving the environment; and to the extent such statutes and
regulations are different from or in conflict with the provisions of this
chapter, said state and federal statutes, rules and regulations shall govern.
(Ord. 2006-9, 8-8-2006)
7-2-14: CREDIT CARD PAYMENT:
The village may accept payment of sewer fees and charges, or payment for any
other purpose to the village by approved credit card. There shall be an
additional two dollar ($2.00) convenience fee paid to the village with any
payment made by credit card. (Ord. 2011-4, 4-26-2011)
CHAPTER 3
STORM WATER DISPOSAL
SECTION:
7-3-1: Restriction
7-3-2: Penalty For Violations
7-3-1: RESTRICTION:
   (A)   No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, exterior
foundation drains, areaway drains, or other sources of surface runoff or ground
water to a building drain or other drain or conduit which in turn is connected
directly or indirectly to a public storm drain, without prior, expressed
approval of the board of trustees. Industrial cooling water or unpolluted
process waters may be discharged, on approval of the board of trustees, to a
storm sewer or natural outlet. (Ord., 11-26-1996)
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to dam up, obstruct, impede or
change the natural course of any swale, ditch, waterway or watercourse, or to
dam up or obstruct any swale, ditch, sewer, drain, culvert or waterway
established as a part of a platted subdivision, or otherwise established by the
president and board of trustees for the purpose of surface or subsurface storm
water drainage; provided that any of the above listed acts shall not be a
violation of this section if expressly approved by the board of trustees. No
person shall install, or cause to be installed, any driveway, sidewalk or other
improvements which cross over any swale, ditch, waterway or watercourse without
providing an adequate means for unobstructed flow of water in said swale,
ditch, waterway or watercourse, as approved by the village. The village may
require culverts, erosion control and approved design and construction. (Ord.
2001-16, 12-11-2001)
   (C)   1. All proposed structures on lots zoned residential and proposed
additions or modifications to said structures or any other changes to said
residential lots shall not alter the existing grade elevations within two and
five-tenths feet (2.5') of side lot boundary lines and five feet (5') of all
front and rear lot boundary lines, unless the permit applicant has demonstrated
to the zoning administrator for the village that such a proposed grade
elevation change is not detrimental to existing site drainage or to that of the
adjacent properties.
      2.   The documentation required for review by the village zoning
administrator shall consist of an alternate drainage plan, drawn to scale, by a
registered professional engineer and accompanied by the supporting
calculations.
      3.   If an alternate drainage plan is approved, the permit applicant or
property owner must provide a copy of a certification from a registered
engineer that the site improvements specified in the alternate drainage plan
are in place and properly constructed. This certification must be received by
the zoning administrator prior to the issuance of any required certificate of
compliance for the structure so as to obtain verification of grades prior to
occupancy of a new structure or addition.
      4.   The alternate drainage plan and/or the engineer's certification
provided for above may only be waived for good cause shown by expressed
approval of the board of trustees.
      5.   In the event of a violation of this subsection (C), the property
owner shall cause the grade elevation of the applicable areas of the said lot
to be returned to its prior elevation within thirty (30) days of receipt of
notice of violation from the village; or said property owner may request a
hearing before the board of trustees, provided said request is received by the
village clerk within fourteen (14) days after the date said notice was mailed
or delivered in person to the property owner.
      6.   In the event the violation of this subsection (C) is not corrected
within said thirty (30) days after the date of said notice or such time allowed
by the board of trustees after a hearing, which shall not be less than thirty
(30) days, the village may cause the said lot grade elevation to be returned to
its prior elevation. The cost of correcting said grade elevation shall be
charged to the property owner. (Ord. 97-12, 11-25-1997)
7-3-2: PENALTY FOR VIOLATIONS:
Any person who violates this chapter shall upon conviction thereof be fined in
accordance with section
1-4-1 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 4
STORM WATER MANAGEMENT
SECTION:
7-4-1: Purpose
7-4-2: Intent
7-4-3: Scope Of Application
7-4-4: Drainage Plan
7-4-5: Drainage System Components
7-4-6: Design Requirements
7-4-7: Protecting Existing Drainage
7-4-7-1: Erosion And Sedimentation Control
7-4-8: Easements
7-4-9: Rule Of Construction
7-4-10: Variances
7-4-11: Submittals
7-4-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this storm water management chapter is to help guide the
attempts of developers to control the transportation or movement of storm water
and reduce damage to property and protect the public health, safety, and
general welfare. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-2: INTENT:
The intent of this storm water management chapter is to require temporary
storage of storm water runoff, to control the rate of release of storm water
runoff, provide for adequate drainage of development sites and surrounding
areas, and protect existing agricultural drainage systems. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-
1999)
7-4-3: SCOPE OF APPLICATION:
   (A)   Reviewing Authority: For the purpose of this chapter the reviewing
authority shall be the village planning commission with final approval by the
village board of trustees for storm water management plans submitted in
connection with a subdivision plat. After initial hearing, further modification
may be approved by the board of trustees only. If no subdivision is involved,
the reviewing authority shall be the board of trustees only. (2005 Code)
   (B)   Applicability: The requirements of this chapter shall apply to the
following:
      1.   All subdivisions which require the approval of the village board of
trustees. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
      2.   Any development of land within the village unless expressly exempted
herein. For purposes of this chapter, "development" shall mean building of any
structures or covering the ground with any material or adding, removing or
movement of soil which significantly changes the runoff pattern of surface
water.
   (C)   Exemptions:
      1.   This policy shall not apply to completed development or completed
construction which has occurred on sites located in subdivisions which were
developed and approved prior to November 9, 1999. (2005 Code)
      2.   Development of a single-family or duplex residential home and
accessory buildings on a lot of less than one-half (1/2) acre in an R-1 or R-
2 residential zoning district. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-4: DRAINAGE PLAN:
   (A)   A storm water drainage plan including a combination of storm water
storage and controlled release shall be required of all development of land
which is subject to the provisions of this chapter. Such storm water drainage
plan must be approved by the village board of trustees after review and
recommendation of the planning commission before development may begin.
   (B)   If it is determined by the board of trustees that said plan does not
meet the requirements of this chapter, or that the village storm water system
does not have adequate capacity to accept storm water from the development
site, then the development plan shall not be approved. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-5: DRAINAGE SYSTEM COMPONENTS:
   (A)   Minor: The minor drainage component of the drainage system shall
consist of storm sewers, street gutters, small open channels, and swales
designed to store and convey the runoff from the 10-year recurrence interval
precipitation event utilizing the Illinois state water bulletin for rainfall
depths. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999; amd. 2005 Code)
   (B)   Major: The major drainage components shall be designed to store and
convey storm water flows beyond the capacity of the minor drainage component.
Information depicting storm water flow paths (including cross sectional data),
velocities, rates, and elevations and maps of flooding shall be included in the
submittal. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-6: DESIGN REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Design Methods:
      1.   Calculation Of Drainage Capacity: The rational method may be used to
size the components of the proposed storm sewer system.
      2.   Calculation Of Required Storage (Watershed Area Less Than Or Equal
To 2,000 Acres): The volume of required storm water storage shall be based on
the following criteria:
         (a)   First flush storm event (0.75 inch rainfall depth). The
detention pond shall be designed to detain the first flush storm event for a
period not less than twenty four (24) hours. The required storage volume for a
first flush storm event shall be calculated as follows:
   Vff = 2,722.5 * C * A
Where:
   C   =   Developed runoff coefficient
A   =   Developed area (in acres)
   Vff   =   First flush volume (in cubic feet)
A restriction shall be designed to limit the first flush storm discharge to a
rate such that the pond will completely discharge in the required time period.
         (b)   2-year storm event. The detention pond shall be designed to
discharge a maximum of 0.04 cfs/developed acre during the 2-year storm event. A
restriction shall be designed to limit the 2-year storm discharge rate. The 2-
year storm restrictor shall be placed at an elevation equal to the first flush
storage elevation.
         (c)   50-year storm event. The detention pond shall be designed to
discharge a maximum of 0.20 cfs/developed acre during the 50-year storm event.
A restriction shall be designed to limit the 50-year storm discharge rate. The
50-year storm restrictor shall be placed at an elevation equal to the 2-year
storage elevation.
      3.   Storm Water Routing Methodologies: The required storage volume and
detention pond routing calculations shall be prepared using a generally
accepted storm water routing analysis, such as HEC-1, HEC-HMS, TR-55, TR-20,
PondPak, or XP-SWMM. Alternate methods of analysis may be considered if their
technical validity and accuracy is demonstrated.
The 10-year high water level shall be calculated using the above methodology
and used to establish the downstream boundary condition for the hydraulic grade
line calculations.
The Huff 3rd quartile 24-hour duration rainfall distribution shall be used for
the 2-year and 50-year detention pond routing calculations.
      4.   Required Freeboard; Detention Pond: A minimum of one vertical foot
of freeboard shall be provided above the 50-year peak water surface elevation.
No building shall be constructed within the proposed storm sewer system with a
first floor elevation less than two (2) vertical feet above the 50-year peak
water surface elevation.
      5.   Off Site Runoff: If storm water runoff enters the proposed
development from another parcel, it shall be demonstrated how this runoff is to
be collected and conveyed. It will be the responsibility of the developer to
provide an adequate and safe flow path for off site runoff.
      6.   Outlet Certification: When a proposed detention pond outlets to an
existing pipe, stream, river, or other drainage facility with a history of
flooding problems, it shall be demonstrated that the water levels in the
receiving system will not adversely affect the hydraulic performance of the
proposed detention pond. If necessary, the proposed detention pond may need to
be raised to a higher elevation so as to avoid the impacts of downstream
hydraulic restrictions.
      7.   Emergency Overflow: An emergency overflow path shall be provided for
each storm water detention facility. This overflow structure shall be
constructed to function without special maintenance and shall not increase the
risk of erosion or endangering public safety. It shall be demonstrated that
discharge from the emergency overflow will have adequate conveyance downstream
of the development.
      8.   Calculation Of Required Storage (Watershed Area Greater Than 2,000
Acres): In the event of a large development (larger than 2,000 acres), the
total area shall be divided into manageable subwatersheds for the purpose of
establishing individual storm water management zones. Each subwatershed shall
be subject to the above storm water conveyance and detention pond sizing
requirements. The size and layout of proposed subwatersheds are subject to
village approval.
   (B)   Storm Water Storage Areas:
      1.   Wet Bottom Detention Pond: The use of wet bottom detention ponds is
recommended, as they help to minimize storm water pollution and provide
positive site amenities. The following requirements shall apply to the design
and construction of wet bottom detention basins:
         (a)   The water surface area of the permanent pool shall not exceed
one-fifth (1/5) of the area of the tributary watershed, or as approved by the
reviewing authority.
         (b)   Minimum normal water depth (excluding safety ledges and side
slopes) shall be eight feet (8') provided, however, that if fish are to be
maintained in the pond at least one-quarter (1/4) of the pond area shall be a
minimum of ten feet (10') deep.
         (c)   Measures shall be included in the design to minimize pond
stagnation and to help ensure adequate aerobic pond conditions.
         (d)   Storage facility side slopes shall provide a safety ledge below
the normal water elevation which shall not exceed a slope of six to one (6:1)
(6 horizontal units to 1 vertical unit) to a point at which the normal water
depth is no less than five feet (5'). Below a normal depth of five feet (5'),
side slopes shall not exceed the stable angle of repose under saturated
conditions of the soil material of the basin.
         (e)   Detention pond discharge pipes less than twelve inches (12") in
diameter shall not be allowed. Multiple discharge pipes from a storm water
storage area are discouraged.
         (f)   It shall be demonstrated that the detention pond discharge pipe
will adequately connect to a receiving system and that the receiving system has
adequate capacity to convey the 50-year peak discharge rate of 0.20 cfs per
developed acre.
         (g)   Warning signs shall be placed at appropriate locations to warn
of deep water, possible flood conditions during storm periods, and other
dangers that exist to pedestrian and vehicular traffic.
      2.   Dry Bottom Detention Pond: A dry bottom detention pond may be
considered only when the construction of a wet detention pond is demonstrated
to be infeasible. Dry bottom detention ponds shall be designed in compliance
with all applicable requirements which govern the construction of wet bottom
detention basins. The following requirements shall apply to the design and
construction of dry bottom detention basins:
         (a)   Dry bottom storm water storage facilities should be designed
where possible to serve a secondary purpose for recreation, open space, or
similar types of uses which will not be adversely affected by occasional
intermittent flooding and will not interfere with storm water management.
         (b)   Minimum grades for turf area within the basin shall be two
percent (2%) (50 units horizontal to 1 unit vertical) except that the minimum
grade shall be one percent (1%) (100 units horizontal to 1 unit vertical) if
tile underdrain is adequately installed underneath the turf areas. Storage
facility side slopes shall not exceed three to one (3:1) (3 units horizontal to
1 unit vertical), shall provide for the reasonably safe approach of persons and
reasonably safe maintenance practices. Side slopes steeper than three to one
(3:1) may be allowed upon a determination by the reviewing authority that
adequate precautions are taken to avoid unreasonable hazard. Storage basin
excavations shall follow the natural land contours as closely as practicable.
The geometry of dry bottom storm water storage basins shall be approved by the
reviewing authority.
         (c)   Temporary seeding, sodding or other soil stabilization measures
as directed by the reviewing authority shall be established in the storm water
storage basin and excess storm water passageway immediately following the
construction or reconstruction of these facilities. During the construction of
the overall development, it is recognized that a limited amount of sediment
buildup may occur in the storm water storage facility due to erosion. In no
case shall the volume of the storage basin be reduced to less than ninety
percent (90%) of the required volume during the construction phase of the
development. Basins may be over excavated to provide additional storage volume
for anticipated sedimentation during construction activities.
         (d)   Permanent erosion control measures such as hydroseeding,
conventional seeding, nurse crops, fertilizing, or sod installation and
associated stabilization techniques such as mulching shall be utilized to
control soil movement and erosion within the storage area and excess storm
water passageway. These measures shall conform to the guidelines established in
the "Procedures And Standards For Urban Soil Erosion And Sedimentation Control
In Illinois". The installation of these permanent measures shall take place
only after the majority of construction and other silt and sediment producing
activities have been completed. Prior to the establishment of permanent erosion
control measures, the required capacity of the storm water storage area and the
excess storm water passageway shall, if necessary, be restored by excavation of
deposited material to provide one hundred percent (100%) of the required
storage volume. Upon completion of construction activities the storage volume
shall be certified in writing by an Illinois registered professional engineer.
The specific erosion control measures to be employed shall be included in an
erosion control plan to be approved by the reviewing authority.
         (e)   The outlet control structure shall be provided with an
interceptor for trash and debris, and it shall be designed and constructed to
minimize soil erosion and not to require manual adjustments for its proper
operation. The control structure shall be designed to operate properly with
minimal maintenance or attention. The control structure shall be provided with
safety screens for any pipe or opening, other than a weir, to prevent children
or large animals from crawling into structures. The control structure shall be
constructed to allow access to it at all times, including times of flood flow.
         (f)   Paved low flow conduits shall be provided in storm water storage
basins. These conduits shall be so constructed that they will not unnecessarily
interfere with any secondary use of the storage area and will reduce the
frequency of time that the storage area will be covered with water. These
conduits shall facilitate dewatering of the soils in the storm water storage
area to avoid saturated soil conditions. Low flow conduits shall facilitate
complete interior drainage of the storm water storage area. Tile underdrain
systems may be combined with the low flow conduits or channel systems.
         (g)   Pipe outlets of less than twelve inches (12") in diameter shall
not be allowed unless specifically approved by the reviewing authority.
Multiple outlet pipes from a storm water storage area shall be avoided.
         (h)   Warning signs shall be placed at appropriate locations to warn
of deep water, possible flood conditions during storm periods, and of other
dangers that exist to pedestrian and vehicular traffic.
      3.   Alternative Storm Water Storage Areas: The use of the storm water
storage facilities as described in this chapter are the preferred means of
storm water storage. The following alternative means of storm water storage may
be used on development sites under two (2) acres in area or where practical
necessity makes the use of conventional storm water storage facilities
infeasible. The use of such alternative storm water storage areas is only
permitted upon the approval of the reviewing authority. Storage of storm water
runoff in public streets will not be allowed.
         (a)   Paved Storm Water Storage: Design and construction of the
pavement base must ensure that there is minimal pavement damage due to
flooding. Control structures in paved areas must be readily accessible for
maintenance and cleaning. Flow control devices will be required unless
otherwise approved by the reviewing authority.
         (b)   Rooftop Storm Water Storage: Rooftop storage of excess storm
water shall be designed and constructed to provide permanent control inlets and
parapet walls to contain excess storm water. Adequate structural roof design
must be provided to ensure that roof deflection does not occur which could
cause the roofing material to fail and result in leakage. Overflow areas must
be provided to ensure that the weight of storm water will never exceed the
structural capacity of the roof. Any rooftop storage of excess storm water
shall be approved only upon submission of building plans signed and sealed by
an Illinois licensed structural engineer or architect attesting to the
structural adequacy of the design.
         (c)   Automobile Parking Lot Storage Areas: Automobile parking lots
may be designed to provide temporary detention storage on a portion of their
surfaces. Automobile parking facilities used to store excess storm water may be
constructed having a maximum depth of stored storm water of 0.6 foot; and these
areas shall be located in the most remote, least used area of the parking
facility. Parking lot storm water detention shall not be permitted in areas
containing handicapped parking areas. Design and construction of automobile
parking in storm water areas must ensure that there is minimal damage to the
parking facility due to flooding, including minimal damage to the subbase.
Warning signs shall be mounted at appropriate locations to warn of possible
flood conditions during storm periods.
         (d)   Underground Storm Water Storage: Underground storm water storage
facilities must be designed for easy access in order to remove accumulated
sediment and debris. These facilities must be provided with a positive gravity
outlet unless otherwise approved by the reviewing authority. (2005 Code)
7-4-7: PROTECTING EXISTING DRAINAGE:
   (A)   Natural Drainage:
      1.   Existing perennial streams shall not be modified to accommodate on
site flows of storm water. Stream banks may be modified, however, incident to
the installation of an excess storm water runoff outfall, necessary to ensure
safety or bank stabilization, and/or for the improvement of aquatic habitats.
      2.   Other natural drainage features such as depressional storage areas
and swales shall be incorporated into the drainage system.
   (B)   Agricultural Drainage Improvements:
      1.   The outlet for existing agricultural drainage tile will be located
and the capacity of the outlet shall be maintained for the watershed upstream
of the development area.
      2.   Existing easements for any agricultural drainage tile located
underneath areas that will be developed shall be preserved. If no easement
exists an easement shall be granted for access and maintenance as provided in
this chapter. Such easements shall be of sufficient width and located to
provide for continued functioning and necessary maintenance of drainage
facilities. No buildings or permanent structures including paved areas but
excluding streets, sidewalks, or driveways, which cross the easement by the
shortest possible route may be located within the easement without the consent
and approval of any public body to which the easement is granted.
      3.   All agricultural drainage tile located underneath areas that will be
developed shall be replaced with nonperforated conduit to prevent root blockage
provided, however, that drainage district tile may remain with the approval of
the drainage district.
      4.   Agricultural drainage tile which, due to development, will be
located underneath roadways, drives, or parking shall be replaced with ductile
iron, or reinforced concrete pipe or equivalent material approved by the
reviewing authority as needed to prevent the collapse of the agricultural
drainage conduit.
      5.   Agricultural drainage tile may be relocated within development areas
upon approval of the reviewing authority. Such relocation shall maintain
sufficient slope and capacity to prevent sedimentation and to prevent an
increase in scouring or structural damage to the conduit. Such relocation shall
only be with the consent and approval of the drainage district, which is
responsible for maintaining the tile. If the tile is not under the authority of
a drainage district the reviewing authority shall consider the interests of
those landowners who are served by the tile.
      6.   No storm sewer inlet, outlet, or detention basin outlet shall be
connected to farm drainage tile unless flow is restricted to an amount equal to
or less than the discharge capacity of the tile. Such connection shall only be
made with the consent and approval of the drainage district responsible for
maintaining the tile. If the tile is not under the authority of a drainage
district the reviewing authority shall consider the interests of those
landowners who are served by the tile.
      7.   No fill shall be placed nor grade altered in such a manner that it
will cause surface water upstream of the development to pond or direct surface
flows in such a way as to create a nuisance.
      8.   All surface runoff water shall exit the development at such a
velocity which will not cause erosion. All subsurface flows shall exit the
development at such a velocity so as to prevent an increase in scouring or
structural damage to off site tile drains.
      9.   Sizing of culvert crossings shall consider entrance and exit losses
as well as tailwater conditions on the culvert. (Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-7-1: EROSION AND SEDIMENTATION CONTROL:
   (A)   The developer shall take such steps as necessary to minimize soil
erosion during and after construction. If there is a threat of erosion, the
village may require an erosion control plan to be submitted with engineering
plans. The erosion control plan shall conform to all applicable portions of the
latest edition of "Procedures And Standards For Urban Soil Erosion And
Sedimentation Control In Illinois". A copy of this publication is available for
inspection at the office of the village engineer. Further, the following
factors shall always be observed during any phase of development construction:
      1.   Natural vegetation should be retained and protected wherever
possible. Areas immediately adjacent to natural watercourses should be left
undisturbed whenever possible.
      2.   The smallest practical area of land should be exposed for the
shortest practical time during development.
      3.   Provisions shall be made to accommodate the increased runoff caused
by changed soil and surface conditions during and after development in
accordance with this chapter.
      4.   Permanent vegetation and structures should be installed as soon as
practical during development. (2005 Code)
7-4-8: EASEMENTS:
Easements to the village, drainage district or other public authority to
provide for maintenance of public drainage facilities which serve the site and
which are or are to be dedicated to, owned by, or under the control of such
public authority shall be granted to further this policy when the need for such
facility is in whole or in part specifically and uniquely attributable to the
proposed development. All known agricultural drainage tile located underneath
areas to be developed shall be granted an easement if no written easement
exists prior to development. Such easement shall be approved in writing by the
public body to which they are granted and recorded in the Champaign County
recorder's office before the reviewing authority issues any final approval
except in the case of subdivisions where such easements are shown on the plat.
(Ord. 99-11, 11-9-1999)
7-4-9: RULE OF CONSTRUCTION:
These policy guidelines shall be construed liberally in the interests of the
public so as to protect the public health, safety, and welfare. (Ord. 99-11,
11-9-1999)
7-4-10: VARIANCES:
The granting of variances is not consistent with the purpose of this chapter.
It is, therefore, essential that every effort be made to comply with the
requirements contained in this chapter.
   (A)   Only the board of trustees may grant a variance. When, in the opinion
of a developer, the standards of this chapter place an undue hardship on a
specific development proposal, the applicant may apply for a variance. The
village engineer shall review the applicant's request, prepare a recommendation
and a public hearing before the planning commission shall be scheduled on the
matter in a manner prescribed by the board of trustees. The board of trustees
shall rule on the variance at its earliest convenience, after the hearing.
   (B)   A variance may be granted by the board of trustees if the applicant
demonstrates all of the following:
      1.   The property cannot yield a reasonable return if the variance is not
granted;
      2.   The relief requested is the minimum necessary;
      3.   There will be no threat to public health and safety or to beneficial
stream uses and functions, especially aquatic habitat, or creation of a
nuisance;
      4.   There will be no additional public expense such as for flood
protection, rescue or relief operations, policing, or repairs to streambeds and
banks, roads, utilities, or other public facilities;
      5.   The applicant's circumstances are unique such that the proposed
variance will not serve as a special privilege, but will alleviate a
demonstrable hardship not shared by other property;
      6.   The granting of the variance will not alter the essential character
of the area involved including existing stream uses;
      7.   All other agency permits have been obtained;
      8.   The applicant did not know or deliberately place himself or herself
in the position of hardship;
      9.   Such other considerations applicable to the particular property as
determined by the board of trustees.
   (C)   The village may require an independent study and report by a qualified
professional engineer or other appropriate qualified professionals, the cost of
which shall be paid by the applicant for the variance. The purpose of the study
shall be to provide evaluations of the applicant's proposed development as they
may affect stream flows and hydraulic characteristics of the watercourse and to
also evaluate possible alternatives to the applicant's proposal. (Ord. 99-11,
11-9-1999)
7-4-11: SUBMITTALS:
   (A)   Storm Water Drainage Plan: Two (2) copies of a storm water drainage
plan and sixteen (16) copies of the site plan prepared by a qualified Illinois
professional engineer must be submitted to the village clerk with any zoning
petition, subdivision application, building permit application or otherwise
prior to development where required by this chapter. Such drainage plan must at
a minimum contain the following:
      1.   Full description of before and after development topography,
existing drainage patterns (including locations of agricultural drainage tile
serving the area to be developed as well as serving off site areas but which
crosses the area to be developed, as well as the efforts to identify and locate
underground tile), grading, and environmental characteristics of the property.
      2.   The potential impacts of the development on storm water resources
both upstream and downstream.
      3.   Erosion control plan.
      4.   An explanation of the minor and major drainage system performance
under storm events up to and including the 100-year precipitation event and of
the provisions for handling drainage from any tributary off site areas.
      5.   Storm water detention system designs. Calculations shall be
submitted with all assumptions, coefficients, and other parameters identified
and their sources noted. The subdivision name or other project identification,
engineer's firm, the engineer's name, and date shall all be indicated. A plot
or tabulation of storage volumes with corresponding water surface elevations
(stage storage table) and of the basin outflow rates for those water surface
(stage discharge) elevations shall be furnished. High water surface elevations
shall be listed for the first flush, 2-year, and 100-year recurrence interval
rainfall events. These tabulations shall be listed for water surface elevation
intervals not exceeding 1.0 foot. Adequate freeboard shall be demonstrated in
these calculations. These calculations shall be located on the site plan. (Ord.
2007-1, 2-27-2007)
   (B)   Certifications: The following certifications shall be submitted prior
to the issuance of any certificate of compliance, final plat approval, or
release of performance guarantee for development on the site as provided in the
applicable provisions of the village zoning and/or subdivision ordinances:
      1.   Certification of storage volume as provided in this chapter.
      2.   As built drawings of the drainage system including the storage
facility in sufficient detail to determine that the constructed facility is
substantially the same as that presented in the approved storm water drainage
plan with certification to that effect by a qualified Illinois professional
engineer.
      3.   Bonds as required by the reviewing authority.
      4.   Warranties as required by the reviewing authority. (Ord. 99-11, 11-
9-1999)
   (C)   Submittals To Be Complete: All submittals required hereunder shall be
submitted to the village clerk and village engineer, in completed form, no less
than two (2) weeks prior to the initial hearing date. Any documents which are
not completed and in form acceptable to the village engineer by two (2) weeks
prior to the hearing date shall result in postponement of the hearing to the
next meeting date. (Ord. 2007-1, 2-27-2007)
CHAPTER 5
POTABLE WATER
SECTION:
7-5-1: Definitions
7-5-2: Use Of Ground Water As A Potable Water Supply Prohibited
7-5-3: Penalties
7-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
PERSON: Any individual, partnership, copartnership, firm, company, limited
liability company, corporation, association, joint stock company, trust,
estate, political subdivision, or any other legal entity, or their legal
representatives, agents or assigns.
POTABLE WATER: Any water used for human or domestic consumption, including, but
not limited to, water used for drinking, bathing, swimming, washing dishes, or
preparing foods. (Ord. 2002-29, 11-26-2002)
7-5-2: USE OF GROUND WATER AS A POTABLE WATER SUPPLY PROHIBITED:
Except for such uses or methods in existence before the effective date hereof,
the use or attempt to use as a potable water supply ground water from within
the corporate limits of the village of St. Joseph by the installation or
drilling of wells or by any other method is hereby prohibited, including at
points of withdrawal by the village of St. Joseph. (Ord. 2002-29, 11-26-2002)
7-5-3: PENALTIES:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to a fine
as provided in title 1 of this code. (Ord. 2002-29, 11-26-2002)
CHAPTER 6
WATER USE RESTRICTION
SECTION:
7-6-1: Authority
7-6-2: Purpose
7-6-3: Declaration Of Policy
7-6-4: Definitions
7-6-5: Application Of Regulations
7-6-6: Declaration Of Water Use Restrictions, Implementation, And Termination
7-6-7: Water Use Restriction Levels
7-6-8: Variance
7-6-9: Violation And Penalty
7-6-10: Severability
7-6-1: AUTHORITY:
   (A)   The authority to impose regulations to restrict the use of water
provided via the public water supply system shall be expressly reserved and may
be amended from time to time, as necessary, by the president and village board
of trustees for the village of St. Joseph. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-2: PURPOSE:
   (A)   This chapter establishes a village water use restriction ordinance for
the village of St. Joseph, Champaign County, Illinois. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-3: DECLARATION OF POLICY:
   (A)   In the event that the Illinois American Water Company (IAWC) district
manager notifies the village regarding a period of high usage, water shortage,
or water emergency, the village shall take measures appropriate to efficiently
safeguard the safety and health of the general public or to provide for the
public convenience. The use of public water supply system water in the village,
or in any portion thereof, for irrigation, cooling, watering or other uses may
be forbidden, restricted, or regulated and such regulations may be made
effective as to all persons using the public water supply system water or as to
particular classes of public water supply system users. Rationing may be
imposed to address an imminent or actual public water supply disruption or
shortage, either in lieu of or in addition to other measures hereby authorized.
(Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-4: DEFINITIONS:
DRIP IRRIGATION SYSTEM: An irrigation system that saves water by allowing water
to drip slowly to the roots of plants, either onto the soil surface or directly
onto the root zone. Such systems include, but are not limited to, soaker hoses.
EVEN NUMBER ADDRESS: A street address ending in 0, 2, 4, 6, 8 or a letter "A" -
"M", or a location without an address.
HANDHELD WATERING DEVICE: A means of watering that requires the watering device
to be held in order to operate, including watering cans, buckets, and hoses
equipped with a spray nozzle and an automatic shutoff valve. Such a hose is a
handheld watering device provided it is continuously attended.
HARVESTED RAINWATER: Water accumulated and stored during times of
precipitation, such as through rain barrels and cistern systems, which is
prevented from entering the stormwater treatment system, and is redirected for
reuse on site.
HIGH USAGE: Period of time during which public water system demand or public
water system supply equals or exceeds public water system treatment production
capacity and potentially threatens system storage capacity and the continued
availability of water for human consumption, sanitation and/or fire protection.
ILLINOIS AMERICAN WATER COMPANY: Shall include its successors.
LANDSCAPE: The area of the property planted with vegetation other than grass.
LAWN: The area of the property planted with grass.
LAWN SPRINKLER: A device attached to a hose designed to allow for the
unattended watering of lawns or landscaping, but does not include a drip
irrigation system.
LAWN WATERING: Any means or methods of applying water to a lawn.
NONESSENTIAL WATER USES: (A) Washing down sidewalks, walkways, driveways,
parking lots, tennis courts, or other hard surface areas.
   (B)   Washing down buildings or structures for purposes other than immediate
fire protection.
   (C)   Flushing gutters or permitting water to run or accumulate in any
gutter or street.
   (D)   Washing any motorbike, motor vehicle, boat, trailer, airplane or other
vehicle, except for public emergency vehicles.
   (E)   Maintaining fountains, reflection ponds, and decorative water bodies
for aesthetic or scenic purposes.
   (F)   Filling or maintaining fill levels in public or private swimming and
wading pools.
   (G)   Watering lawns, plants, trees, and other flora on private or public
property, except as otherwise provided under this chapter.
   (H)   Serving water routinely in restaurants.
   (I)   Increasing water levels in scenic and recreational ponds and lakes.
   (J)   Irrigating golf courses except greens, tees, and fairways.
   (K)   Obtaining water from hydrants for any purpose other than firefighting.
ODD NUMBER ADDRESS: A street address ending in 1, 3, 5, 7, 9 or a letter "N" -
"Z".
PERSON: Any individual, partnership, copartnership, firm, company, limited
liability company, corporation, association, joint stock company, trust,
estate, political subdivision, or any other legal entity, or their legal
representatives, agents, or assigns.
PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY SYSTEM: Shall include water supplied by the Illinois
American Water Company, or its successors. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-5: APPLICATION OF REGULATIONS:
   (A)   The provisions of this chapter shall apply to any person using water
within the village, and
      1.   The property is supplied by village's public water supply system,
regardless of whether the property is located within the municipal boundaries
of village; and
      2.   The property is located within the specific area identified in the
alert or declaration.
   (B)   Emergency service providers in the act of providing emergency service
shall be exempt from provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-6: DECLARATION OF WATER USE RESTRICTIONS, IMPLEMENTATION, AND TERMINATION:
   (A)   Upon receiving notification from the IAWC district manager, or
designee, explaining the justifiable need for a level 1 voluntary water use
restriction alert, level 2 mandatory water use restriction declaration, or
level 3 emergency water use restriction declaration, and within twenty four
(24) hours or on the next business day, the president, or any designee, shall:
      1.   Declare or rescind a level 1 voluntary water use restriction alert;
or
      2.   Recommend to the village board of trustees that:
         (a)   A level 2 mandatory water use restriction declaration or level 3
emergency water use restriction declaration be declared or rescinded; or
         (b)   A change to or from a level 2 mandatory water use restriction
declaration or level 3 emergency water use restriction declaration is declared.
   (B)   Upon the declaration of, or upon the rescinding of, a:
Level 1 voluntary water use restriction alert,
Level 2 mandatory water use restriction declaration, or
Level 3 emergency water use restriction declaration,
the president, or any designee, shall take actions necessary to notify all
public water supply users and the general public of the appropriate response
actions and practices, including, but not limited to, notifying broadcast media
outlets and emergency alert messaging systems as appropriate.
   (C)   Mandatory water use restriction provisions shall take effect
immediately upon the issuance of public notification of a level 2 mandatory
water use restriction declaration, or level 3 emergency water use restriction
declaration. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-7: WATER USE RESTRICTION LEVELS:
   (A)   Levels: The village establishes three (3) levels of water use
restrictions to address an imminent or actual public water supply disruption or
shortage, as indicated in table 7.1 of this section. The water use restriction
levels are based on IAWC Champaign district measurements of water supply, water
demand, and water system conditions, such as days of remaining storage, water
demand as a percent of supply, or water quality indicators.
      TABLE 7.1
      DESCRIPTION OF WATER USE RESTRICTION LEVELS
 
Level 1   Conditions indicate potential for public water supply shortages.
Voluntary Voluntary water conservation is encouraged.
Level 2   Water supplies are measurably lower than the seasonal norm and are
Mandatory diminishing. Mandatory restriction measures are imposed.
Level 3   The public water supply system is experiencing a water shortage and
Emergency treated water supply is clearly inadequate. More stringent
          restriction measures must be imposed.
 
   (B)   Level 1 Voluntary Water Use Restriction Alert:
      1.   During a level 1 voluntary water use restriction alert, the
following voluntary actions by all persons (residential, institutional,
commercial, and industrial) are recommended, but not mandated:
         (a)   Stop nonessential water uses.
         (b)   Use rain barrels to collect and store water from roof drains,
and use this water for garden irrigation and lawn irrigation.
         (c)   If watering a lawn, set timers to run the system before ten
o'clock (10:00) A.M. or after five o'clock (5:00) P.M. to reduce water loss
through evaporation during the heat of the day.
         (d)   Use drip irrigation hoses to water garden plants and landscape
plants, trees, and shrubs at the roots.
         (e)   Install water and energy efficient appliances.
         (f)   Wash dishes and clothes only when appliance is full.
         (g)   Regularly check and repair toilets, faucets, water pipes, and
outdoor hoses for leaks.
   (C)   Level 2 Mandatory Water Use Restriction Measures:
      1.   During a level 2 mandatory water use restriction declaration, all
persons (residential, institutional, commercial, and industrial) shall adhere
to the following required public water supply system water use restrictions:
         (a)   All persons shall cease nonessential water uses.
         (b)   All persons shall adhere to the following schedule if a lawn is
to be watered:
(1) All properties with an even number address may use water for lawn watering
only on even numbered calendar dates between the hours of six o'clock (6:00)
A.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. or between the hours of six o'clock (6:00)
P.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) P.M.
(2) All properties with an odd number address may use water for lawn watering
only on odd numbered calendar dates between the hours of six o'clock (6:00)
A.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. or between the hours of six o'clock (6:00)
P.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) P.M.
      2.   During a level 2 mandatory water use restriction declaration, there
shall be no restrictions as to hours or days when water may be used for any of
the following:
         (a)   The watering of sod on the initial day of sod installation;
         (b)   Lawn watering where such watering is done using harvested
rainwater;
         (c)   The watering of landscape, such as trees, shrubs, flowers and
gardens, with a handheld hose not larger than one inch (1") diameter or by
means of an automatic root feed or drip irrigation system;
         (d)   Lawn watering where such watering is done with the proper,
attended use of a handheld watering device;
         (e)   Vehicle or equipment washing, provided that all water hoses in
use are equipped with an automatic shutoff valve or spray nozzle which shuts
off automatically; or
         (f)   Any other lawful use of water such as bathing, clothes washing,
or other normal household uses not otherwise specifically restricted by the
provisions of this section.
   (D)   Level 3 Emergency Water Use Restriction Measures:
      1.   During a level 3 emergency water use restriction declaration, all
persons (residential, institutional, commercial, and industrial) shall adhere
to the following required public water supply system water use restrictions:
         (a)   All persons shall cease nonessential water uses.
         (b)   The use of automatic water sprinklers and other remote water
broadcast devices shall be prohibited.
         (c)   The use of aesthetic fountains that do not operate on recycled
water shall be prohibited.
         (d)   Persons shall be prohibited from using public water supply to
fill swimming pools, water slides that do not recycle, or for other related
recreational water consuming activities. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-8: VARIANCE:
   (A)   A person may request a variance from a mandatory level 2 or level 3
water use restriction requirement from the president, or designee, on a form
provided for that purpose within seven (7) days after such restriction becomes
effective, provided that compliance with such mandatory water use restriction
would result in serious health, safety, or economic hardship to that person.
   (B)   In order for a variance to be granted, the petitioner must show one or
more of the following conditions:
      1.   Compliance with this chapter cannot be technically accomplished
within the duration of the water use restriction declaration.
      2.   Alternate methods can be implemented which will achieve the same
level of reduction in water use.
   (C)   The president may, in writing, grant temporary variances for existing
water uses otherwise prohibited under this chapter if it is determined that
failure to grant such variances would cause an emergency condition adversely
affecting health, sanitation, or fire protection for the public or the
petitioner and if one or more aforementioned conditions in subsection (B) of
this section is met. Any such variance so ratified may be revoked by later
action of the president.
   (D)   Any such variance denied by the president can be appealed to the
village board of trustees at a public hearing.
      1.   No such variance shall be retroactive or otherwise justify any
violation of this chapter occurring prior to the issuance of the variance.
      2.   A fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) shall be paid to the village to
offset costs of providing notice of the public hearing.
      3.   A variance granted by the village board of trustees shall be subject
to the following conditions, unless waived or modified by the village board of
trustees:
         (a)   Variances granted shall include a timetable for compliance.
         (b)   Variances granted shall expire when the water use restriction
declaration has been rescinded, unless the petitioner has failed to meet
specified requirements. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-9: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
   (A)   It shall be the duty of president, or designee, to investigate
violations of the mandatory restrictions and to issue and post a notice of
violation consistent with the purpose and intent of this chapter.
   (B)   Any person who violates, disobeys, neglects, fails to comply with, or
resists enforcement of the mandatory provisions of this chapter shall, within
ten (10) days of receiving a notice of violation, as indicated in subsection
(A) of this section, be subject to the following administrative penalties:
 
First violation  $ 50.00 per occurrence
Second violation 100.00 per occurrence
Third violation  200.00 per occurrence
 
   (C)   Each day upon which there is a violation shall be deemed to be a
separate occurrence. Payment of said administrative penalty shall be made to
the village within ten (10) days of receipt of the notice of violation. (Ord.
2013-7, 8-13-2013)
7-6-10: SEVERABILITY:
In the event that any portion of this chapter is held to be unconstitutional
for any reason, the remaining portions of this chapter shall not be affected.
The provisions of this chapter shall prevail and control in the event of any
inconsistency between this chapter and other rules and regulations of the
village and/or state of Illinois. (Ord. 2013-7, 8-13-2013)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Obstructing Streets, Sidewalks
8-1-2: Moving Buildings; Permit Required
8-1-3: Excavations
8-1-4: Remove Grade Stakes
8-1-5: Dirt Removal
8-1-6: Rural Mailboxes
8-1-7: Specific Streets As Part Of Street System
8-1-8: Street Specifications
8-1-9: Sidewalk Specifications
8-1-10: Sidewalk Protection During Construction
8-1-11: Small Wireless Facilities
8-1-1: OBSTRUCTING STREETS, SIDEWALKS:
   (A)   Building Or Other Materials: It shall be unlawful for any builder or
other person to encumber or obstruct any street, sidewalk or alley within the
Village with any building materials, equipment or other like articles without
written permission from the President of the Board of Trustees.
   (B)   Rubbish, Dirt, Filth: No person shall obstruct or encumber any street,
alley or sidewalk with rubbish, dirt or other articles of property, upon any
such street, alley or sidewalk longer than may be necessary for the prompt
removal of the same.
   (C)   Obstruction Of Street Or Alley: It shall be unlawful for any person to
obstruct any street or alley within the Village by unnecessarily stopping
thereon with any automobile, vehicle, trailer or other chattel, so as to
interfere with persons or vehicles using the same.
   (D)   Temporary Merchandise On Right-Of-Way: It shall be unlawful for any
person or entity to place, hang or set out over or upon any Village sidewalk,
any goods, wares or merchandise, except temporarily within two feet (2') of the
premises or building occupied by him/her/it or to place, suspend or erect any
sign, showbill, showcase, flag or other obstruction, projecting into or hanging
over any sidewalk exceeding two feet (2') from the building or premises
occupied by him/her/it, or to knowingly permit the same to be done or continue
in front of any building or premises owned or occupied by him/her/it or under
his/her/its control.
   (E)   Encroachments: No person or entity shall make or cause to be made any
erection, enclosure, or obstruction encroaching in whole or in part upon or
over any street, alley or sidewalk within the Village without permission from
the Board of Trustees.
   (F)   Notice; Removal: The owner of any erection or enclosure already
erected or placed without permission of the Board of Trustees and encroaching
upon or over any street or alley within the Village, shall remove the same
within thirty (30) days after notice by the President of the Board of Trustees.
   (G)   Cost Of Removal: The President may cause any encumbrance, obstruction,
erection or enclosure in, over or upon any street, alley or sidewalk contrary
to this chapter to be removed and the costs of such removal shall be paid by
the person or entity causing such obstruction.
   (H)   Liability For Damages: Any person who shall place or leave, or cause
to be placed or left, any encroachment, encumbrance or obstruction in, over or
upon any street, alley or sidewalk within the Village shall in all cases be
liable to the Village for all damages or injury arising from such encroachment,
encumbrance or obstruction.
   (I)   Authorized Obstructions: Any obstruction or encroachment upon or over
a Village sidewalk, alley or street authorized by this chapter or by permission
of the Board of Trustees shall in all instances be a license revocable at any
time by the Board of Trustees. Any such obstructions or encroachments shall
leave adequate and safe space for the public use of such sidewalk, alley or
street. Any such structures shall be erected in a good, safe and sound manner.
All approved awnings must be at least eight feet (8') above the sidewalk. (2005
Code)
8-1-2: MOVING BUILDINGS; PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall move or cause to be removed, or aid in removing any building
through or across any street or alley within the Village without written
permission from the Board of Trustees, nor shall in removing such building
unnecessarily encumber or obstruct any street or alley, nor for a longer time
than may be necessary in the prompt and diligent removal of such building.
(2005 Code)
8-1-3: EXCAVATIONS:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to excavate, strip, undermine or
in any manner dig away any public street, alley, sidewalk, right of way, or any
part of any public street, alley, sidewalk or right of way within the village
unless authorized as provided hereafter.
   (B)   No person or entity shall make any excavation in any village street,
alley, sidewalk or right of way without written permission from the village
president or, in his absence, the village superintendent of public works. Any
person or entity acting by or under such permission as aforesaid, making or
causing to be made any excavation or ditch for any purpose in any street,
alley, sidewalk or right of way shall, without any unnecessary delay, cause the
same to be filled and compacted to the proper level of the street, alley,
sidewalk or right of way, and finish the surface as required by this code or by
the board of trustees and upon completion remove all equipment, excess
materials and debris; and shall leave said site in the same or as good
condition as before said work began; and shall from time to time, if necessary,
continue to repair the same until the earth is completely settled and the
surface conforms to the proper level of the street, alley, sidewalk or right of
way.
   (C)   Any person or entity tearing up or in any manner injuring any street,
sidewalk, bridge, culvert or vegetation within the village for any purpose, or
negligently breaking or injuring the same by the removing of any building over
the same, or otherwise, shall without delay cause such street, sidewalk,
bridge, culvert, or vegetation to be repaired and placed in the same or as good
condition as before the breaking or injuring thereof.
   (D)   Utility excavations shall be in accordance with the following
requirements:
      1.   All street cut trenches made either to existing pavements or
sidewalks or future pavement areas shall be backfilled utilizing one of two (2)
recommended methods: those being the use of controlled low strength materials
(CLSM) or, alternately, the placement of mechanically compacted lifts, six inch
(6") maximum, of CA6 or CA10 aggregate materials as approved by the village.
CLSM material shall be in accordance with section 593 of the Illinois
department of transportation "Standard Specifications For Road And Bridge
Construction".
The use of FA6 aggregate material, commonly known as "turkey grit", as backfill
will be permitted as approved by the village president. Water inundation or
jetting of the fine aggregate backfill material will not be permitted. The
proper backfill shall extend not less than two feet (2') in each direction
beyond the edge of the pavement.
      2.   When a trench is cut into an existing concrete street or sidewalk,
the pavement shall be replaced in kind with a total thickness two inches (2")
greater than existing to a maximum of ten inches (10"). When restoring concrete
pavement, the entire slab into which the trench was cut shall be removed and
replaced.
If the surface is either asphalt or oil and chip, a six inch (6") thick
concrete pavement shall be installed and two inches (2") of hot mix asphalt
surface course shall be placed atop the concrete base. The use of full depth
integrally colored concrete pavement will be permitted as approved by the
village. Replacement pavement shall be installed no less than a distance of two
feet (2') in each direction beyond the edge of the excavation trench.
      3.   All utility structures (i.e., shutoff valves, vault boxes, lids,
poles, lines, markers, etc.) that pose a threat to public safety shall be
replaced when directed by the village. Any failures occurring outside of the
original restored or repaired pavement or right of way area resulting from the
utility activity will be repaired by the responsible utility company.
      4.   Any person, firm, corporation or entity which plans to install any
underground utilities within a present or proposed street or sidewalk right of
way area is required to notify the village a minimum of twenty four (24) hours
prior to beginning work, except in the case of an emergency. The notification
shall include the exact location and nature of the work to be performed.
Roadway or sidewalk area repairs or restorations made without proper
notification may require reexcavation and replacement with approved backfill.
In emergency situations, the village shall be notified immediately upon the
responsible party's decision that excavation is required.
      5.   Variance from any of the utility excavation policy provisions as
